Both are pushed onto the mark stack.\n    56→class G1TaskQueueEntry {\n    57→private:\n    58→  void* _holder;\n    59→\n    60→  static const uintptr_t ArraySliceBit = 1;\n    61→\n    62→  G1TaskQueueEntry(oop obj) : _holder(obj) {\n    63→    assert(_holder != nullptr, \"Not allowed to set null task queue element\");\n    64→  }\n    65→  G1TaskQueueEntry(HeapWord* addr) : _holder((void*)((uintptr_t)addr | ArraySliceBit)) { }\n    66→public:\n    67→\n    68→  G1TaskQueueEntry() : _holder(nullptr) { }\n    69→  // Trivially copyable, for use in GenericTaskQueue.\n    70→\n    71→  static G1TaskQueueEntry from_slice(HeapWord* what) { return G1TaskQueueEntry(what); }\n    72→  static G1TaskQueueEntry from_oop(oop obj) { return G1TaskQueueEntry(obj); }\n    73→\n    74→  oop obj() const {\n    75→    assert(!is_array_slice(), \"Trying to read array slice \" PTR_FORMAT \" as oop\", p2i(_holder));\n    76→    return cast_to_oop(_holder);\n    77→  }\n    78→\n    79→  HeapWord* slice() const {\n    80→    assert(is_array_slice(), \"Trying to read oop \" PTR_FORMAT \" as array slice\", p2i(_holder));\n    81→    return (HeapWord*)((uintptr_t)_holder & ~ArraySliceBit);\n    82→  }\n    83→\n    84→  bool is_oop() const { return !is_array_slice(); }\n    85→  bool is_array_slice() const { return ((uintptr_t)_holder & ArraySliceBit) != 0; }\n    86→  bool is_null() const { return _holder == nullptr; }\n    87→};\n    88→\n    89→typedef GenericTaskQueue<G1TaskQueueEntry, mtGC> G1CMTaskQueue;\n    90→typedef GenericTaskQueueSet<G1CMTaskQueue, mtGC> G1CMTaskQueueSet;\n    91→\n    92→// Closure used by CM during concurrent reference discovery\n    93→// and reference processing (during remarking) to determine\n    94→// if a particular object is alive. An instance is also embedded into the\n    97→// reference processor as the _is_alive_non_header field\n    98→class G1CMIsAliveClosure : public BoolObjectClosure {\n    99→  G1ConcurrentMark* _cm;\n   100→\n   101→public:\n   102→  G1CMIsAliveClosure();\n   103→  G1CMIsAliveClosure(G1ConcurrentMark* cm);\n   104→  void initialize(G1ConcurrentMark* cm);\n   105→\n   106→  bool do_object_b(oop obj);\n   107→};\n   108→\n   109→class G1CMSubjectToDiscoveryClosure : public BoolObjectClosure {\n   110→  G1CollectedHeap* _g1h;\n   111→public:\n   112→  G1CMSubjectToDiscoveryClosure(G1CollectedHeap* g1h) : _g1h(g1h) { }\n   113→  bool do_object_b(oop obj);\n   114→};\n   115→\n   116→// Represents the overflow mark stack used by concurrent marking.\n   117→//\n   118→// Stores oops in a huge buffer in virtual memory that is always fully committed.\n   119→// Resizing may only happen during a STW pause when the stack is empty.\n   120→//\n   121→// Memory is allocated on a \"chunk\" basis, i.e. a set of oops. For this, the mark\n   122→// stack memory is split into evenly sized chunks of oops. Users can only\n   123→// add or remove entries on that basis.\n   124→// Chunks are filled in increasing address order. Not completely filled chunks\n   125→// have a null element as a terminating element.\n   126→//\n   127→// Every chunk has a header containing a single pointer element used for memory\n   128→// management. This wastes some space, but is negligible (< .1% with current sizing).\n   129→//\n   130→// Memory management is done using a mix of tracking a high water-mark indicating\n   131→// that all chunks at a lower address are valid chunks, and a singly linked free\n   132→// list connecting all empty chunks.\n   133→class G1CMMarkStack {\n   134→public:\n   135→  // Number of TaskQueueEntries that can fit in a single chunk.\n   136→  static const size_t EntriesPerChunk = 1024 - 1 /* One reference for the next pointer */;\n   137→private:\n   138→  struct TaskQueueEntryChunk {\n   139→    TaskQueueEntryChunk* next;\n   140→    G1TaskQueueEntry data[EntriesPerChunk];\n   141→  };\n   142→\n   143→  class ChunkAllocator {\n   144→    // The chunk allocator relies on a growable array data structure that allows resizing without the\n   145→    // need to copy existing items. The basic approach involves organizing the array into chunks,\n   146→    // essentially creating an \"array of arrays\"; referred to as buckets in this implementation. To\n   147→    // facilitate efficient indexing, the size of the first bucket is set to a power of 2. This choice\n   148→    // allows for quick conversion of an array index into a bucket index and the corresponding offset\n   149→    // within the bucket. Additionally, each new bucket added to the growable array doubles the capacity of\n   150→    // the growable array.\n   151→    //\n   152→    // Illustration of the growable array data structure.\n   153→    //\n   154→    //        +----+        +----+----+\n   155→    //        |    |------->|    |    |\n   156→    //        |    |        +----+----+\n   157→    //        +----+        +----+----+\n   158→    //        |    |------->|    |    |\n   159→    //        |    |        +----+----+\n   160→    //        +----+        +-----+-----+-----+-----+\n   161→    //        |    |------->|     |     |     |     |\n   162→    //        |    |        +-----+-----+-----+-----+\n   163→    //        +----+        +-----+-----+-----+-----+-----+-----+-----+----+\n   164→    //        |    |------->|     |     |     |     |     |     |     |    |\n   165→    //        |    |        +-----+-----+-----+-----+-----+-----+-----+----+\n   166→    //        +----+\n   167→    //\n   168→    size_t _min_capacity;\n   169→    size_t _max_capacity;\n   170→    size_t _capacity;\n   171→    size_t _num_buckets;\n   172→    bool _should_grow;\n   173→    TaskQueueEntryChunk* volatile* _buckets;\n   174→    char _pad0[DEFAULT_PADDING_SIZE];\n   175→    volatile size_t _size;\n   176→    char _pad4[DEFAULT_PADDING_SIZE - sizeof(size_t)];\n   177→\n   178→    size_t bucket_size(size_t bucket) {\n   179→      return (bucket == 0) ?\n   180→              _min_capacity :\n   181→              _min_capacity * ( 1ULL << (bucket - 1));\n   182→    }\n   183→\n   184→    static unsigned int find_highest_bit(uintptr_t mask) {\n   185→      return count_leading_zeros(mask) ^ (BitsPerWord - 1U);\n   186→    }\n   187→\n   188→    size_t get_bucket(size_t array_idx) {\n   189→      if (array_idx < _min_capacity) {\n   190→        return 0;\n   191→      }\n   192→\n   193→      return find_highest_bit(array_idx) - find_highest_bit(_min_capacity) + 1;\n   194→    }\n   195→\n   196→    size_t get_bucket_index(size_t array_idx) {\n   197→      if (array_idx < _min_capacity) {\n   198→        return array_idx;\n   199→      }\n   200→      return array_idx - (1ULL << find_highest_bit(array_idx));\n   201→    }\n   202→\n   203→    bool reserve(size_t new_capacity);\n   204→\n   205→  public:\n   206→    ChunkAllocator();\n   207→\n   208→    ~ChunkAllocator();\n   209→\n   210→    bool initialize(size_t initial_capacity, size_t max_capacity);\n   211→\n   212→    void reset() {\n   213→      _size = 0;\n   214→      _should_grow = false;\n   215→    }\n   216→\n   217→    // During G1CMConcurrentMarkingTask or finalize_marking phases, we prefer to restart the marking when\n   218→    // the G1CMMarkStack overflows. Attempts to expand the G1CMMarkStack should be followed with a restart\n   219→    // of the marking. On failure to allocate a new chuck, the caller just returns and forces a restart.\n   220→    // This approach offers better memory utilization for the G1CMMarkStack, as each iteration of the\n   221→    // marking potentially involves traversing fewer unmarked nodes in the graph.\n   222→\n   223→    // However, during the reference processing phase, instead of restarting the marking process, the\n   224→    // G1CMMarkStack is expanded upon failure to allocate a new chunk. The decision between these two\n   225→    // modes of expansion is determined by the _should_grow parameter.\n   226→    void set_should_grow() {\n   227→      _should_grow = true;\n   228→    }\n   229→\n   230→    size_t capacity() const { return _capacity; }\n   231→\n   232→    // Expand the mark stack doubling its size.\n   233→    bool try_expand();\n   234→    bool try_expand_to(size_t desired_capacity);\n   235→\n   236→    TaskQueueEntryChunk* allocate_new_chunk();\n   237→  };\n   238→\n   239→  ChunkAllocator _chunk_allocator;\n   240→\n   241→  char _pad0[DEFAULT_PADDING_SIZE];\n   242→  TaskQueueEntryChunk* volatile _free_list;  // Linked list of free chunks that can be allocated by users.\n   243→  char _pad1[DEFAULT_PADDING_SIZE - sizeof(TaskQueueEntryChunk*)];\n   244→  TaskQueueEntryChunk* volatile _chunk_list; // List of chunks currently containing data.\n   245→  volatile size_t _chunks_in_chunk_list;\n   246→  char _pad2[DEFAULT_PADDING_SIZE - sizeof(TaskQueueEntryChunk*) - sizeof(size_t)];\n   247→\n   248→  // Atomically add the given chunk to the list.\n   249→  void add_chunk_to_list(TaskQueueEntryChunk* volatile* list, TaskQueueEntryChunk* elem);\n   250→  // Atomically remove and return a chunk from the given list. Returns null if the\n   251→  // list is empty.\n   252→  TaskQueueEntryChunk* remove_chunk_from_list(TaskQueueEntryChunk* volatile* list);\n   253→\n   254→  void add_chunk_to_chunk_list(TaskQueueEntryChunk* elem);\n   255→  void add_chunk_to_free_list(TaskQueueEntryChunk* elem);\n   256→\n   257→  TaskQueueEntryChunk* remove_chunk_from_chunk_list();\n   258→  TaskQueueEntryChunk* remove_chunk_from_free_list();\n   259→\n   260→ public:\n   261→  G1CMMarkStack();\n   262→  ~G1CMMarkStack() = default;\n   263→\n   264→  // Alignment and minimum capacity of this mark stack in number of oops.\n   265→  static size_t capacity_alignment();\n   266→\n   267→  // Allocate and initialize the mark stack.\n   268→  bool initialize();\n   269→\n   270→  // Pushes the given buffer containing at most EntriesPerChunk elements on the mark\n   271→  // stack. If less than EntriesPerChunk elements are to be pushed, the array must\n   272→  // be terminated with a null.\n   273→  // Returns whether the buffer contents were successfully pushed to the global mark\n   274→  // stack.\n   275→  bool par_push_chunk(G1TaskQueueEntry* buffer);\n   276→\n   277→  // Pops a chunk from this mark stack, copying them into the given buffer. This\n   278→  // chunk may contain up to EntriesPerChunk elements. If there are less, the last\n   279→  // element in the array is a null pointer.\n   280→  bool par_pop_chunk(G1TaskQueueEntry* buffer);\n   281→\n   282→  // Return whether the chunk list is empty. Racy due to unsynchronized access to\n   283→  // _chunk_list.\n   284→  bool is_empty() const { return _chunk_list == nullptr; }\n   285→\n   286→  size_t capacity() const  { return _chunk_allocator.capacity(); }\n   287→\n   288→  void set_should_grow() {\n   289→    _chunk_allocator.set_should_grow();\n   290→  }\n   291→\n   292→  // Expand the stack, typically in response to an overflow condition\n   293→  void expand();\n   294→\n   295→  // Return the approximate number of oops on this mark stack. Racy due to\n   296→  // unsynchronized access to _chunks_in_chunk_list.\n   297→  size_t size() const { return _chunks_in_chunk_list * EntriesPerChunk; }\n   298→\n   299→  void set_empty();\n   300→\n   301→  // Apply Fn to every oop on the mark stack. The mark stack must not\n   302→  // be modified while iterating.\n   303→  template<typename Fn> void iterate(Fn fn) const PRODUCT_RETURN;\n   304→};\n   305→\n   306→// Root MemRegions are memory areas that contain objects which references are\n   307→// roots wrt to the marking. They must be scanned before marking to maintain the\n   308→// SATB invariant.\n   309→// Typically they contain the areas from TAMS to top of the regions.\n   310→// We could scan and mark through these objects during the concurrent start pause,\n   311→// but for pause time reasons we move this work to the concurrent phase.\n   312→// We need to complete this procedure before we can evacuate a particular region\n   313→// because evacuation might determine that some of these \"root objects\" are dead,\n   314→// potentially dropping some required references.\n   315→// Root MemRegions comprise of the contents of survivor regions at the end\n   316→// of the GC, and any objects copied into the old gen during GC.\n   317→class G1CMRootMemRegions {\n   318→  // The set of root MemRegions.\n   319→  MemRegion* _root_regions;\n   320→  size_t const _max_regions;\n   321→\n   322→  volatile size_t _num_root_regions; // Actual number of root regions.\n   323→\n   324→  volatile size_t _claimed_root_regions; // Number of root regions currently claimed.\n   325→\n   326→  volatile bool _scan_in_progress;\n   327→  volatile bool _should_abort;\n   328→\n   329→  void notify_scan_done();\n   330→\n   331→public:\n   332→  G1CMRootMemRegions(uint const max_regions);\n   333→  ~G1CMRootMemRegions();\n   334→\n   335→  // Reset the data structure to allow addition of new root regions.\n   336→  void reset();\n   337→\n   338→  void add(HeapWord* start, HeapWord* end);\n   339→\n   340→  // Reset the claiming / scanning of the root regions.\n   341→  void prepare_for_scan();\n   342→\n   343→  // Forces get_next() to return null so that the iteration aborts early.\n   344→  void abort() { _should_abort = true; }\n   345→\n   346→  // Return true if the CM thread are actively scanning root regions,\n   347→  // false otherwise.\n   348→  bool scan_in_progress() { return _scan_in_progress; }\n   349→\n   350→  // Claim the next root MemRegion to scan atomically, or return null if\n   351→  // all have been claimed.\n   352→  const MemRegion* claim_next();\n   353→\n   354→  // The number of root regions to scan.\n   355→  uint num_root_regions() const;\n   356→\n   357→  // Is the given memregion contained in the root regions; the MemRegion must\n   358→  // match exactly.\n   359→  bool contains(const MemRegion mr) const;\n   360→\n   361→  void cancel_scan();\n   362→\n   363→  // Flag that we're done with root region scanning and notify anyone\n   364→  // who's waiting on it. If aborted is false, assume that all regions\n   365→  // have been claimed.\n   366→  void scan_finished();\n   367→\n   368→  // If CM threads are still scanning root regions, wait until they\n   369→  // are done. Return true if we had to wait, false otherwise.\n   370→  bool wait_until_scan_finished();\n   371→};\n   372→\n   373→// This class manages data structures and methods for doing liveness analysis in\n   374→// G1's concurrent cycle.\n   375→class G1ConcurrentMark : public CHeapObj<mtGC> {\n   376→  friend class G1CMBitMapClosure;\n   377→  friend class G1CMConcurrentMarkingTask;\n   378→  friend class G1CMDrainMarkingStackClosure;\n   379→  friend class G1CMKeepAliveAndDrainClosure;\n   380→  friend class G1CMRefProcProxyTask;\n   381→  friend class G1CMRemarkTask;\n   382→  friend class G1CMRootRegionScanTask;\n   383→  friend class G1CMTask;\n   384→  friend class G1ConcurrentMarkThread;\n   385→\n   386→  G1ConcurrentMarkThread* _cm_thread;     // The thread doing the work\n   387→  G1CollectedHeap*        _g1h;           // The heap\n   388→\n   389→  // Concurrent marking support structures\n   390→  G1CMBitMap              _mark_bitmap;\n   391→\n   392→  // Heap bounds\n   393→  MemRegion const         _heap;\n   394→\n   395→  // Root region tracking and claiming\n   396→  G1CMRootMemRegions      _root_regions;\n   397→\n   398→  // For grey objects\n   399→  G1CMMarkStack           _global_mark_stack;    // Maximum number of marking tasks\n   406→  uint                    _num_active_tasks; // Number of tasks currently active\n   407→  G1CMTask**              _tasks;            // Task queue array (max_worker_id length)\n   408→\n   409→  G1CMTaskQueueSet*       _task_queues; // Task queue set\n   410→  TaskTerminator          _terminator;  // For termination\n   411→\n   412→  // Two sync barriers that are used to synchronize tasks when an\n   413→  // overflow occurs. The algorithm is the following. All tasks enter\n   414→  // the first one to ensure that they have all stopped manipulating\n   415→  // the global data structures. After they exit it, they re-initialize\n   416→  // their data structures and task 0 re-initializes the global data\n   417→  // structures. Then, they enter the second sync barrier. This\n   418→  // ensure, that no task starts doing work before all data\n   419→  // structures (local and global) have been re-initialized. When they\n   420→  // exit it, they are free to start working again.\n   421→  WorkerThreadsBarrierSync     _first_overflow_barrier_sync;\n   422→  WorkerThreadsBarrierSync     _second_overflow_barrier_sync;\n   423→\n   424→  // Number of completed mark cycles.\n   425→  volatile uint           _completed_mark_cycles;\n   426→\n   427→  // This is set by any task, when an overflow on the global data\n   428→  // structures is detected\n   429→  volatile bool           _has_overflown;\n   430→  // True: marking is concurrent, false: we're in remark\n   431→  volatile bool           _concurrent;\n   432→  // Set at the end of a Full GC so that marking aborts\n   433→  volatile bool           _has_aborted;\n   434→\n   435→  // Used when remark aborts due to an overflow to indicate that\n   436→  // another concurrent marking phase should start\n   437→  volatile bool           _restart_for_overflow;\n   438→\n   439→  ConcurrentGCTimer*      _gc_timer_cm;\n   440→\n   441→  G1OldTracer*            _gc_tracer_cm;\n   442→\n   443→  // Timing statistics. It might return null if the next region is empty or\n   498→  // we have run out of regions. In the latter case, out_of_regions()\n   499→  // determines whether we've really run out of regions or the task\n   500→  // should call claim_region() again. This might seem a bit\n   501→  // awkward. Originally, the code was written so that claim_region()\n   502→  // either successfully returned with a non-empty region or there\n   503→  // were no more regions to be claimed. The problem with this was\n   504→  // that, in certain circumstances, it iterated over large chunks of\n   505→  // the heap finding only empty regions and, while it was working, it\n   506→  // was preventing the calling task to call its regular clock\n   507→  // method. So, this way, each task will spend very little time in\n   508→  // claim_region() and is allowed to call the regular clock method\n   509→  // frequently.\n   510→  G1HeapRegion* claim_region(uint worker_id);\n   511→\n   512→  // Determines whether we've run out of regions to scan. Both are pushed onto the mark stack.\nclass G1TaskQueueEntry {\nprivate:\n  void* _holder;\n\n  static const uintptr_t ArraySliceBit = 1;\n\n  G1TaskQueueEntry(oop obj) : _holder(obj) {\n    assert(_holder != nullptr, \"Not allowed to set null task queue element\");\n  }\n  G1TaskQueueEntry(HeapWord* addr) : _holder((void*)((uintptr_t)addr | ArraySliceBit)) { }\npublic:\n\n  G1TaskQueueEntry() : _holder(nullptr) { }\n  // Trivially copyable, for use in GenericTaskQueue.\n\n  static G1TaskQueueEntry from_slice(HeapWord* what) { return G1TaskQueueEntry(what); }\n  static G1TaskQueueEntry from_oop(oop obj) { return G1TaskQueueEntry(obj); }\n\n  oop obj() const {\n    assert(!is_array_slice(), \"Trying to read array slice \" PTR_FORMAT \" as oop\", p2i(_holder));\n    return cast_to_oop(_holder);\n  }\n\n  HeapWord* slice() const {\n    assert(is_array_slice(), \"Trying to read oop \" PTR_FORMAT \" as array slice\", p2i(_holder));\n    return (HeapWord*)((uintptr_t)_holder & ~ArraySliceBit);\n  }\n\n  bool is_oop() const { return !is_array_slice(); }\n  bool is_array_slice() const { return ((uintptr_t)_holder & ArraySliceBit) != 0; }\n  bool is_null() const { return _holder == nullptr; }\n};\n\ntypedef GenericTaskQueue<G1TaskQueueEntry, mtGC> G1CMTaskQueue;\ntypedef GenericTaskQueueSet<G1CMTaskQueue, mtGC> G1CMTaskQueueSet;\n\n// Closure used by CM during concurrent reference discovery\n// and reference processing (during remarking) to determine\n// if a particular object is alive. It is primarily used\n// to determine if referents of discovered reference objects\n// are alive. An instance is also embedded into the\n// reference processor as the _is_alive_non_header field\nclass G1CMIsAliveClosure : public BoolObjectClosure {\n  G1ConcurrentMark* _cm;\n\npublic:\n  G1CMIsAliveClosure();\n  G1CMIsAliveClosure(G1ConcurrentMark* cm);\n  void initialize(G1ConcurrentMark* cm);\n\n  bool do_object_b(oop obj);\n};\n\nclass G1CMSubjectToDiscoveryClosure : public BoolObjectClosure {\n  G1CollectedHeap* _g1h;\npublic:\n  G1CMSubjectToDiscoveryClosure(G1CollectedHeap* g1h) : _g1h(g1h) { }\n  bool do_object_b(oop obj);\n};\n\n// Represents the overflow mark stack used by concurrent marking.\n//\n// Stores oops in a huge buffer in virtual memory that is always fully committed.\n// Resizing may only happen during a STW pause when the stack is empty.\n//\n// Memory is allocated on a \"chunk\" basis, i.e. a set of oops. For this, the mark\n// stack memory is split into evenly sized chunks of oops. Users can only\n// add or remove entries on that basis.\n// Chunks are filled in increasing address order. Not completely filled chunks\n// have a null element as a terminating element.\n//\n// Every chunk has a header containing a single pointer element used for memory\n// management. This wastes some space, but is negligible (< .1% with current sizing).\n//\n// Memory management is done using a mix of tracking a high water-mark indicating\n// that all chunks at a lower address are valid chunks, and a singly linked free\n// list connecting all empty chunks.\nclass G1CMMarkStack {\npublic:\n  // Number of TaskQueueEntries that can fit in a single chunk.\n  static const size_t EntriesPerChunk = 1024 - 1 /* One reference for the next pointer */;\nprivate:\n  struct TaskQueueEntryChunk {\n    TaskQueueEntryChunk* next;\n    G1TaskQueueEntry data[EntriesPerChunk];\n  };\n\n  class ChunkAllocator {\n    // The chunk allocator relies on a growable array data structure that allows resizing without the\n    // need to copy existing items. The basic approach involves organizing the array into chunks,\n    // essentially creating an \"array of arrays\"; referred to as buckets in this implementation. To\n    // facilitate efficient indexing, the size of the first bucket is set to a power of 2. This choice\n    // allows for quick conversion of an array index into a bucket index and the corresponding offset\n    // within the bucket. Additionally, each new bucket added to the growable array doubles the capacity of\n    // the growable array.\n    //\n    // Illustration of the growable array data structure.\n    //\n    //        +----+        +----+----+\n    //        |    |------->|    |    |\n    //        |    |        +----+----+\n    //        +----+        +----+----+\n    //        |    |------->|    |    |\n    //        |    |        +----+----+\n    //        +----+        +-----+-----+-----+-----+\n    //        |    |------->|     |     |     |     |\n    //        |    |        +-----+-----+-----+-----+\n    //        +----+        +-----+-----+-----+-----+-----+-----+-----+----+\n    //        |    |------->|     |     |     |     |     |     |     |    |\n    //        |    |        +-----+-----+-----+-----+-----+-----+-----+----+\n    //        +----+\n    //\n    size_t _min_capacity;\n    size_t _max_capacity;\n    size_t _capacity;\n    size_t _num_buckets;\n    bool _should_grow;\n    TaskQueueEntryChunk* volatile* _buckets;\n    char _pad0[DEFAULT_PADDING_SIZE];\n    volatile size_t _size;\n    char _pad4[DEFAULT_PADDING_SIZE - sizeof(size_t)];\n\n    size_t bucket_size(size_t bucket) {\n      return (bucket == 0) ?\n              _min_capacity :\n              _min_capacity * ( 1ULL << (bucket - 1));\n    }\n\n    static unsigned int find_highest_bit(uintptr_t mask) {\n      return count_leading_zeros(mask) ^ (BitsPerWord - 1U);\n    }\n\n    size_t get_bucket(size_t array_idx) {\n      if (array_idx < _min_capacity) {\n        return 0;\n      }\n\n      return find_highest_bit(array_idx) - find_highest_bit(_min_capacity) + 1;\n    }\n\n    size_t get_bucket_index(size_t array_idx) {\n      if (array_idx < _min_capacity) {\n        return array_idx;\n      }\n      return array_idx - (1ULL << find_highest_bit(array_idx));\n    }\n\n    bool reserve(size_t new_capacity);\n\n  public:\n    ChunkAllocator();\n\n    ~ChunkAllocator();\n\n    bool initialize(size_t initial_capacity, size_t max_capacity);\n\n    void reset() {\n      _size = 0;\n      _should_grow = false;\n    }\n\n    // During G1CMConcurrentMarkingTask or finalize_marking phases, we prefer to restart the marking when\n    // the G1CMMarkStack overflows. Attempts to expand the G1CMMarkStack should be followed with a restart\n    // of the marking. On failure to allocate a new chuck, the caller just returns and forces a restart.\n    // This approach offers better memory utilization for the G1CMMarkStack, as each iteration of the\n    // marking potentially involves traversing fewer unmarked nodes in the graph.\n\n    // However, during the reference processing phase, instead of restarting the marking process, the\n    // G1CMMarkStack is expanded upon failure to allocate a new chunk. The decision between these two\n    // modes of expansion is determined by the _should_grow parameter.\n    void set_should_grow() {\n      _should_grow = true;\n    }\n\n    size_t capacity() const { return _capacity; }\n\n    // Expand the mark stack doubling its size.\n    bool try_expand();\n    bool try_expand_to(size_t desired_capacity);\n\n    TaskQueueEntryChunk* allocate_new_chunk();\n  };\n\n  ChunkAllocator _chunk_allocator;\n\n  char _pad0[DEFAULT_PADDING_SIZE];\n  TaskQueueEntryChunk* volatile _free_list;  // Linked list of free chunks that can be allocated by users.\n  char _pad1[DEFAULT_PADDING_SIZE - sizeof(TaskQueueEntryChunk*)];\n  TaskQueueEntryChunk* volatile _chunk_list; // List of chunks currently containing data.\n  volatile size_t _chunks_in_chunk_list;\n  char _pad2[DEFAULT_PADDING_SIZE - sizeof(TaskQueueEntryChunk*) - sizeof(size_t)];\n\n  // Atomically add the given chunk to the list.\n  void add_chunk_to_list(TaskQueueEntryChunk* volatile* list, TaskQueueEntryChunk* elem);\n  // Atomically remove and return a chunk from the given list. Returns null if the\n  // list is empty.\n  TaskQueueEntryChunk* remove_chunk_from_list(TaskQueueEntryChunk* volatile* list);\n\n  void add_chunk_to_chunk_list(TaskQueueEntryChunk* elem);\n  void add_chunk_to_free_list(TaskQueueEntryChunk* elem);\n\n  TaskQueueEntryChunk* remove_chunk_from_chunk_list();\n  TaskQueueEntryChunk* remove_chunk_from_free_list();\n\n public:\n  G1CMMarkStack();\n  ~G1CMMarkStack() = default;\n\n  // Alignment and minimum capacity of this mark stack in number of oops.\n  static size_t capacity_alignment();\n\n  // Allocate and initialize the mark stack.\n  bool initialize();\n\n  // Pushes the given buffer containing at most EntriesPerChunk elements on the mark\n  // stack. If less than EntriesPerChunk elements are to be pushed, the array must\n  // be terminated with a null.\n  // Returns whether the buffer contents were successfully pushed to the global mark\n  // stack.\n  bool par_push_chunk(G1TaskQueueEntry* buffer);\n\n  // Pops a chunk from this mark stack, copying them into the given buffer. This\n  // chunk may contain up to EntriesPerChunk elements. If there are less, the last\n  // element in the array is a null pointer.\n  bool par_pop_chunk(G1TaskQueueEntry* buffer);\n\n  // Return whether the chunk list is empty. Racy due to unsynchronized access to\n  // _chunk_list.\n  bool is_empty() const { return _chunk_list == nullptr; }\n\n  size_t capacity() const  { return _chunk_allocator.capacity(); }\n\n  void set_should_grow() {\n    _chunk_allocator.set_should_grow();\n  }\n\n  // Expand the stack, typically in response to an overflow condition\n  void expand();\n\n  // Return the approximate number of oops on this mark stack. Racy due to\n  // unsynchronized access to _chunks_in_chunk_list.\n  size_t size() const { return _chunks_in_chunk_list * EntriesPerChunk; }\n\n  void set_empty();\n\n  // Apply Fn to every oop on the mark stack. The mark stack must not\n  // be modified while iterating.\n  template<typename Fn> void iterate(Fn fn) const PRODUCT_RETURN;\n};\n\n// Root MemRegions are memory areas that contain objects which references are\n// roots wrt to the marking. They must be scanned before marking to maintain the\n// SATB invariant.\n// Typically they contain the areas from TAMS to top of the regions.\n// We could scan and mark through these objects during the concurrent start pause,\n// but for pause time reasons we move this work to the concurrent phase.\n// We need to complete this procedure before we can evacuate a particular region\n// because evacuation might determine that some of these \"root objects\" are dead,\n// potentially dropping some required references.\n// Root MemRegions comprise of the contents of survivor regions at the end\n// of the GC, and any objects copied into the old gen during GC.\nclass G1CMRootMemRegions {\n  // The set of root MemRegions.\n  MemRegion* _root_regions;\n  size_t const _max_regions;\n\n  volatile size_t _num_root_regions; // Actual number of root regions.\n\n  volatile size_t _claimed_root_regions; // Number of root regions currently claimed.\n\n  volatile bool _scan_in_progress;\n  volatile bool _should_abort;\n\n  void notify_scan_done();\n\npublic:\n  G1CMRootMemRegions(uint const max_regions);\n  ~G1CMRootMemRegions();\n\n  // Reset the data structure to allow addition of new root regions.\n  void reset();\n\n  void add(HeapWord* start, HeapWord* end);\n\n  // Reset the claiming / scanning of the root regions.\n  void prepare_for_scan();\n\n  // Forces get_next() to return null so that the iteration aborts early.\n  void abort() { _should_abort = true; }\n\n  // Return true if the CM thread are actively scanning root regions,\n  // false otherwise.\n  bool scan_in_progress() { return _scan_in_progress; }\n\n  // Claim the next root MemRegion to scan atomically, or return null if\n  // all have been claimed.\n  const MemRegion* claim_next();\n\n  // The number of root regions to scan.\n  uint num_root_regions() const;\n\n  // Is the given memregion contained in the root regions; Return true if we had to wait, false otherwise.\n  bool wait_until_scan_finished();\n};\n\n// This class manages data structures and methods for doing liveness analysis in\n// G1's concurrent cycle.\nclass G1ConcurrentMark : public CHeapObj<mtGC> {\n  friend class G1CMBitMapClosure;\n  friend class G1CMConcurrentMarkingTask;\n  friend class G1CMDrainMarkingStackClosure;\n  friend class G1CMKeepAliveAndDrainClosure;\n  friend class G1CMRefProcProxyTask;\n  friend class G1CMRemarkTask;\n  friend class G1CMRootRegionScanTask;\n  friend class G1CMTask;\n  friend class G1ConcurrentMarkThread;\n\n  G1ConcurrentMarkThread* _cm_thread;     // The thread doing the work\n  G1CollectedHeap*        _g1h;           // The heap\n\n  // Concurrent marking support structures\n  G1CMBitMap              _mark_bitmap;\n\n  // Heap bounds\n  MemRegion const         _heap;\n\n  // Root region tracking and claiming\n  G1CMRootMemRegions      _root_regions;\n\n  // For grey objects\n  G1CMMarkStack           _global_mark_stack; // Grey objects behind global finger\n  HeapWord* volatile      _finger;            // The global finger, region aligned,\n                                              // always pointing to the end of the\n                                              // last claimed region\n\n  uint                    _worker_id_offset;\n  uint                    _max_num_tasks;    // Maximum number of marking tasks\n  uint                    _num_active_tasks; // Number of tasks currently active\n  G1CMTask**              _tasks;            // Task queue array (max_worker_id length)\n\n  G1CMTaskQueueSet*       _task_queues; // Task queue set\n  TaskTerminator          _terminator;  // For termination\n\n  // Two sync barriers that are used to synchronize tasks when an\n  // overflow occurs. The algorithm is the following. All tasks enter\n  // the first one to ensure that they have all stopped manipulating\n  // the global data structures. After they exit it, they re-initialize\n  // their data structures and task 0 re-initializes the global data\n  // structures. Then, they enter the second sync barrier. This\n  // ensure, that no task starts doing work before all data\n  // structures (local and global) have been re-initialized. When they\n  // exit it, they are free to start working again.\n  WorkerThreadsBarrierSync     _first_overflow_barrier_sync;\n  WorkerThreadsBarrierSync     _second_overflow_barrier_sync;\n\n  // Number of completed mark cycles.\n  volatile uint           _completed_mark_cycles;\n\n  // This is set by any task, when an overflow on the global data\n  // structures is detected\n  volatile bool           _has_overflown;\n  // True: marking is concurrent, false: we're in remark\n  volatile bool           _concurrent;\n  // Set at the end of a Full GC so that marking aborts\n  volatile bool           _has_aborted;\n\n  // Used when remark aborts due to an overflow to indicate that\n  // another concurrent marking phase should start\n  volatile bool           _restart_for_overflow;\n\n  ConcurrentGCTimer*      _gc_timer_cm;\n\n  G1OldTracer*            _gc_tracer_cm;\n\n  // Timing statistics. All of them are in ms\n  NumberSeq _remark_times;\n  NumberSeq _remark_mark_times;\n  NumberSeq _remark_weak_ref_times;\n  NumberSeq _cleanup_times;\n\n  double*   _accum_task_vtime;   // Accumulated task vtime\n\n  WorkerThreads* _concurrent_workers;\n  uint      _num_concurrent_workers; // The number of marking worker threads we're using\n  uint      _max_concurrent_workers; // Maximum number of marking worker threads\n\n  enum class VerifyLocation {\n    RemarkBefore,\n    RemarkAfter,\n    RemarkOverflow,\n    CleanupBefore,\n    CleanupAfter\n  };\n  static const char* verify_location_string(VerifyLocation location);\n  void verify_during_pause(G1HeapVerifier::G1VerifyType type,\n                           VerifyLocation location);\n\n  void finalize_marking();\n\n  void weak_refs_work();\n\n  // After reclaiming empty regions, update heap sizes.\n  void compute_new_sizes();\n\n  // Resets all the marking data structures. Called when we have to restart\n  // marking or when marking completes (via set_non_marking_state below).\n  void reset_marking_for_restart();\n\n  // We do this after we're done with marking so that the marking data\n  // structures are initialized to a sensible and predictable state.\n  void reset_at_marking_complete();\n\n  // Called to indicate how many threads are currently active.\n  void set_concurrency(uint active_tasks);\n\n  // Should be called to indicate which phase we're in (concurrent\n  // mark or remark) and how many threads are currently active.\n  void set_concurrency_and_phase(uint active_tasks, bool concurrent);\n\n  // Prints all gathered CM-related statistics\n  void print_stats();\n\n  HeapWord*           finger()       { return _finger;   }\n  bool                concurrent()   { return _concurrent; }\n  uint                active_tasks() { return _num_active_tasks; }\n  TaskTerminator*     terminator()   { return &_terminator; }\n\n  // Claims the next available region to be scanned by a marking\n  // task/thread. It might return null if the next region is empty or\n  // we have run out of regions. In the latter case, out_of_regions()\n  // determines whether we've really run out of regions or the task\n  // should call claim_region() again. This might seem a bit\n  // awkward. Originally, the code was written so that claim_region()\n  // either successfully returned with a non-empty region or there\n  // were no more regions to be claimed. The problem with this was\n  // that, in certain circumstances, it iterated over large chunks of\n  // the heap finding only empty regions and, while it was working, it\n  // was preventing the calling task to call its regular clock\n  // method. So, this way, each task will spend very little time in\n  // claim_region() and is allowed to call the regular clock method\n  // frequently.\n  G1HeapRegion* claim_region(uint worker_id);\n\n  // Determines whether we've run out of regions to scan. Note that\n  // the finger can point past the heap end in case the heap was expanded\n  // to satisfy an allocation without doing a GC. This is fine, because all\n  // objects in those regions will be considered live anyway because of\n  // SATB guarantees (i.e. their TAMS will be equal to bottom).\n  bool out_of_regions() { return _finger >= _heap.end(); }\n\n  // Returns the task with the given id\n  G1CMTask* task(uint id) {\n    // During concurrent start we use the parallel gc threads to do some work, so\n    // we can only compare against _max_num_tasks.\n    assert(id < _max_num_tasks, \"Task id %u not within bounds up to %u\", id, _max_num_tasks);\n    return _tasks[id];\n  }\n\n  // Access / manipulation of the overflow flag which is set to\n  // indicate that the global stack has overflown\n  bool has_overflown()           { return _has_overflown; }\n  void set_has_overflown()       { _has_overflown = true; }\n  void clear_has_overflown()     { _has_overflown = false; }\n  bool restart_for_overflow()    { return _restart_for_overflow; }\n\n  // Methods to enter the two overflow sync barriers\n  void enter_first_sync_barrier(uint worker_id);\n  void enter_second_sync_barrier(uint worker_id);\n\n  // Clear the next marking bitmap in parallel using the given WorkerThreads. We should\n      // not consider those for collection before we fill them up as the effective\n      // gain from them is small. I.e. we only actually reclaim from the filled part,\n      // as the remainder is still eligible for allocation. These objects are also\n      // likely to have already survived a few collections, so they might be longer\n      // lived anyway.\n      // Otherwise the Old region must satisfy the liveness condition.\n      bool should_add = !G1CollectedHeap::heap()->is_old_gc_alloc_region(r) &&\n                        G1CollectionSetChooser::region_occupancy_low_enough_for_evac(r->live_bytes());\n      if (should_add) {\n        add_region(r);\n      } else {\n        r->rem_set()->clear(true /* only_cardset */);\n      }\n      return false;\n    }\n\n    uint regions_added() const { return _regions_added; }\n  };\n\n  G1CollectedHeap* _g1h;\n  G1HeapRegionClaimer _hrclaimer;\n\n  uint volatile _num_regions_added;\n\n  G1BuildCandidateArray _result;\n\n  void update_totals(uint num_regions) {\n    if (num_regions > 0) {\n      Atomic::add(&_num_regions_added, num_regions);\n    }\n  }\n\n  // Early prune (remove) regions meeting the G1HeapWastePercent criteria. That\n  // is, either until only the minimum amount of old collection set regions are\n  // available (for forward progress in evacuation) or the waste accumulated by the\n  // removed regions is above the maximum allowed waste.\n  // Updates number of candidates and reclaimable bytes given.\n  void prune(CandidateInfo* data) {\n    G1Policy* p = G1CollectedHeap::heap()->policy();\n\n    uint num_candidates = Atomic::load(&_num_regions_added);\n\n    uint min_old_cset_length = p->calc_min_old_cset_length(num_candidates);\n    uint num_pruned = 0;\n    size_t wasted_bytes = 0;\n\n    if (min_old_cset_length >= num_candidates) {\n      // We take all of the candidate regions to provide some forward progress.\n      return;\n    }\n\n    size_t allowed_waste = p->allowed_waste_in_collection_set();\n    uint max_to_prune = num_candidates - min_old_cset_length;\n\n    while (true) {\n      G1HeapRegion* r = data[num_candidates - num_pruned - 1]._r;\n allowed_waste);\n\n    Atomic::sub(&_num_regions_added, num_pruned, memory_order_relaxed);\n  }\n\npublic:\n  G1BuildCandidateRegionsTask(uint max_num_regions, uint chunk_size, uint num_workers) :\n
